â€‹

Source: IRS and the [Tax Foundation](https://files.taxfoundation.org/20180207142513/TaxFoundation-FF567-Updated.pdf)

A bit on how all this fits together:

- â–ª[Ordinary income tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/ordinary-income-tax-and-short-term-capital-gains-tax) applies in the situations youâ€™re probably already familiar with, where you pay taxes on [salaries or wages](https://www.irs.gov/taxtopics/tc401.html). Tax rates are based on [filing status](https://www.irs.gov/newsroom/choosing-the-correct-filing-status) (if you are single, married, or support a family), and on which [**income bracket**](https://taxfoundation.org/2018-tax-brackets) you fall under.
- â–ª

**[Income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) brackets.** For [ordinary income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains), as of the **2018** tax year, there are income brackets at **10%**, **12%**, **22%**, **24%**, **32%**, **35%**, and **37%**  [marginal tax rates](http://www.investopedia.com/terms/m/marginaltaxrate.asp)â€”see [Notice 1036](https://www.irs.gov/pub/irs-pdf/n1036.pdf) or a Tax Foundation [summary](https://files.taxfoundation.org/20180207142513/TaxFoundation-FF567-Updated.pdf). Be sure you understand how these brackets work, and what bracket youâ€™re likely to be in.

    - â–«â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-task-finger-bandage' data-evernote-id='217' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)confusionâ€‹ There is a popular misconception that if you move to a higher bracket, youâ€™ll make less money.[*](https://today.yougov.com/news/2013/01/08/understanding-how-marginal-taxes-work-its-all-part/) What actually happens is when you cross certain thresholds, each additional (marginal) dollar you make is taxed at a slightly higher rate, equal to the bracket youâ€™re in. After you earn more than your deduction, on which you pay no tax, your post-tax income looks like the diagram above. (More discussion on such misconceptions are in [this Reddit thread](https://www.reddit.com/r/personalfinance/comments/2wkbgz/graphing_one_misconception_about_tax_brackets/).)
- â–ªInvestment gains, such as buying and selling a stock, are similarly taxed at â€œordinaryâ€ rates, unless they are [**long-term**](https://www.irs.gov/taxtopics/tc409.html), which means you held the asset for more than a year.
- â–ª

You also pay a number of other federal taxes (see a â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-download-thick-box' data-evernote-id='218' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)documentâ€‹[2018 summary for all states](https://www.adp.com/tools-and-resources/compliance-connection/state-taxes/2018-fast-wage-and-tax-facts.aspx)), notably:

    - â–«**6.2%** for Social Security on your first $118,500
    - â–«**1.45%** for Medicare
    - â–«**0.9%**  [Additional Medicare Tax](https://www.irs.gov/Businesses/Small-Businesses-&-Self-Employed/Questions-and-Answers-for-the-Additional-Medicare-Tax) on [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) over $200,000 (single) or $250,000 (married filing jointly)
    - â–«**3.8%**  [Net Investment Income Tax](https://www.irs.gov/uac/Newsroom/Net-Investment-Income-Tax-FAQs) (NII) (enacted as part of the Affordable Care Act,[*](https://www.taxpolicycenter.org/briefing-book/what-tax-changes-did-affordable-care-act-make) also called â€œObamacareâ€) on investment income if you make over $200,000 (single) or $250,000 (married filing jointly).[*](https://www.investopedia.com/articles/personal-finance/020714/new-taxes-under-affordable-care-act.asp)
- â–ªOrdinary federal [income tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-tax), Social Security, and Medicare taxes are withheld from your paycheck by your employer and are called [**employment taxes**](https://www.irs.gov/Businesses/Small-Businesses-&-Self-Employed/Understanding-Employment-Taxes).
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='219' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹  [Long-term capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-and-short-term-capital-gains) are taxed at a lower rate than [ordinary income tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/ordinary-income-tax-and-short-term-capital-gains-tax): **0%**, **15%**, or **20%**.[*](https://www.fool.com/taxes/2017/12/11/long-term-capital-gains-tax-rates-in-2018.aspx) This covers cases where you get [dividends](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/dividend) or sell stock after holding it a year. If you are in the middle brackets (more than about $37K and less than $413K of ordinary income), your long-term capital gains rate is 15%. You can find more detail on tax brackets at the [Tax Foundation](https://taxfoundation.org/2018-tax-brackets/).
- â–ª[AMT](http://fairmark.com/general-taxation/alternative-minimum-tax/alternative-minimum-tax-101/) is a [complex part](https://www.irs.gov/taxtopics/tc556.html) of the federal tax code most taxpayers donâ€™t worry about. But it comes into play when [exercising ISOsÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/the-amt-trap). Most people do not pay [AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) unless it is â€œtriggeredâ€ by specific [situations](https://www.marketwatch.com/story/meet-the-new-friendlier-alternative-minimum-tax-2018-02-26), typically high [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) (more than $500K) or high deductions. Whether you pay AMT also depends on the state in which you file, since your state taxes can significantly affect your deductions. If you are affected, AMT tax rates are usually at **26%** or **28%** marginal tax rate, but effectively **35%** for some ranges, meaning it is higher than [ordinary income tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/ordinary-income-tax-and-short-term-capital-gains-tax) for some incomes and lower for others.[*](https://www.fool.com/taxes/2018/02/05/how-the-alternative-minimum-tax-is-changing-in-201.aspx) AMT rules are so complicated you often need professional tax help if they might apply to you. The IRSâ€™s [AMT Assistant](https://www.irs.gov/Businesses/Small-Businesses-&-Self-Employed/Alternative-Minimum-Tax-(AMT)-Assistant-for-Individuals) might also help.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='220' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹  [Section 1202](https://www.investopedia.com/terms/s/section-1202.asp) of the Internal Revenue Code provides a special tax break for qualified small business stock held for more than five years.[*](https://blog.wealthfront.com/qualified-small-business-stock-2016/) Currently, this tax break is a 100% exclusion from [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) for up to $10M in gain. There are also special rules that enable you to rollover gain on qualified small business stock you have held for less than five years. Stock received on the [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) of options can qualify for the Section 1202 stock benefit.

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

### State Taxes

State tax rates and rules [vary significantly](https://taxfoundation.org/state-individual-income-tax-rates-brackets-2018/). Since federal rates are much higher than state rates, you usually think of federal tax planning first. But you should also know a bit about tax rates in your state.

State [long-term capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-and-short-term-capital-gains) rates range widely. California has the highest, at **13.3%**; several states have none.[*](http://www.fool.com/personal-finance/taxes/2014/10/04/the-states-with-the-highest-capital-gains-tax-rate.aspx)

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='221' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹ For this reason, some people even [consider moving](https://www.forbes.com/sites/robertwood/2016/05/17/can-you-avoid-california-taxes-by-moving/#316bd9471694) to another state if they are likely to have a windfall gain, like selling a lot of stock after an [IPO](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/initial-public-offering-or-ipo-and-goes-public).

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

## [Taxes on Equity Compensation](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/taxes-on-equity-compensation)19 minutes, 29 links

Equity and taxes interact in complicated ways, and the tax consequences for an employee receiving [restricted stock](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants), [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options), or [RSUs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-units-or-rsus) are dramatically different. This section will cover these messy details and help you make decisions that reduce the tax burden of your equity compensation.

Sign up for Good Work

Get the Sunday Delivery and discounts to Holloway Guides only available to Good Work subscribers.

Emails may include promotional content from Holloway. You may opt out at any time.

### 83(b) Elections

This section covers one of the most important and complex decisions you may need to make regarding [stock awards](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants) and [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options): paying taxes early with an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election).

- â–ªGenerally, [restricted stock](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants) is taxed as [ordinary income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains)  [*when it vests*](http://www.investopedia.com/articles/tax/09/restricted-stock-tax.asp?performancelayout=true).
- â–ªIf the stock is in a startup with low value, this may not result in high tax. If itâ€™s been years since the stock was first granted and the company is now worth a lot, the taxes owed could be quite significant.

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ The Internal Revenue Code, in [Section 83(b)](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/26/83), offers taxpayers receiving equity in exchange for work the option to pay taxes on their options before they vest. If qualified, a person can tell the IRS they prefer this alternative in a process called an [**83(b) election**](http://acceleratedvesting.com/what-is-an-83b-election-and-when-do-i-make-it-part-1-with-graphic/). Paying taxes early with an 83(b) election can potentially reduce taxes significantly. If the shares go up in value, the taxes owed at [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting) might be far greater than the taxes owed at the time of receipt.

- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-task-finger-bandage' data-evernote-id='222' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)confusionâ€‹ Why is it called an *election*? Because you are *electing* (choosing) to pay taxes early in exchange for this treatment by the IRS. Does the IRS secretly enjoy making simple concepts sound confusing? Weâ€™re not sure.
- â–ªAn 83(b) election isnâ€™t guaranteed to reduce your taxes, however. For example, the value of the stock may not increase. And if you leave the company before you vest, you *donâ€™t* get back the taxes youâ€™ve already paid.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='223' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ You must file the 83(b) election yourself with the IRS [**within 30 days**](https://www.irs.gov/irb/2012-28_IRB/ar12.html) of the grant or [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise), or the opportunity is irrevocably lost.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-task-finger-bandage' data-evernote-id='224' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)confusionâ€‹ Note an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election) is made on receipt of actual shares of stock. Technically, it cannot be made on the receipt of a stock *option* itself: You first must [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) that option, then file the election.
- â–ªIf you receive an early exercisable [stock option](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) (when you donâ€™t have to wait for the the stock to vest), you can make an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election) upon receipt of the exercised shares.
- â–ªSection [83(b) elections](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election) do not apply to vested shares; the election only applies to stock that is not yet vested. Thus, if you receive options that are *not* early exercisable (meaning you have to wait until they vest to exercise), an 83(b) election would not apply.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='225' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹ Founders and very early employees will almost always want to do an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election) upon the receipt of unvested shares, since the stock value is probably low. If the value is really low, and the taxes owed are not that great, you can make the election without having to pay much tax and start your [capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) holding period on the shares.

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-new-circle' data-evernote-id='226' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)newâ€‹ With the passage of the [Tax Cuts and Jobs Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_Cuts_and_Jobs_Act_of_2017) (TCJA) in 2017, Congress approved a [**new Section 83(i)**](https://www.wsgr.com/WSGR/Display.aspx?SectionName=publications/PDFSearch/wsgralert-section-83i.htm) that is intended to allow deferral of tax until RSU and [stock option](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) holders can sell shares to pay the tax bill. Whether companies will choose or be able to make this available to employees is [not clear](http://stockoptioncounsel.com/blog/tax-deferred-option-exercises-under-the-new-section-83i-tax-cuts-and-jobs-act-of-2017) yet.

### 409A Valuations

When a personâ€™s stock vests, or they [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) an option, the IRS determines the tax that person owes. But if no one is buying and selling stock, as is the case in most startups, then the value of the stockâ€”and thus any tax owed on itâ€”is not obvious.

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ The **fair market value (FMV)** of any good or property refers to a price upon which the buyer and seller have agreed, when both parties are willing, knowledgeable, and not under direct pressure to carry out the exchange. The fair market value of a companyâ€™s stock refers to the price at which a company will issue stock to its employees, and is used by the IRS to calculate how much tax an employee owes on any equity compensation they receive. The FMV of a companyâ€™s stock is determined by the companyâ€™s most recent 409A valuation.

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ A [**409A valuation**](http://www.fenwick.com/FenwickDocuments/409_Valuations_Stock_Options.pdf) is an assessment [private companies](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies) are required by the IRS to conduct regarding the value of any equity the company issues or offers to employees. A company wants the 409A to be low, so that employees make more off options, but not so low the IRS wonâ€™t consider it reasonable. In order to minimize the risk that a 409A [valuation](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/valuation) is manipulated to the benefit of the company, companies hire independent firms to perform 409A valuations, typically annually or after events like [fundraising](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/fundraising-and-financing).

The 409A valuation of employee equity is usually much less than what investors pay for [preferred stock](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/common-stock-and-preferred-stock); often, it might be only a third or less of the preferred stock price.

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-natural-disaster-hurricane' data-evernote-id='227' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)controversyâ€‹ Although the 409A process is required and completely standard for startups, the practice is a strange mix of formality and complete guesswork. It has been called â€œquite preciseâ€”remarkably inaccurate,â€ by [venture capitalist](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/venture-capital-and-venture-capitalists-or-vcs) Bill Gurley. You can read more about its [nuances and controversies](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/03/08/business/dealbook/valuation-shell-game-silicon-valleys-dirty-secret.html).

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

- â–ª

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-sigma' data-evernote-id='228' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)technicalâ€‹ â€œFMVâ€ is a legal term defined in Supreme Court Case 546, [United States vs. Cartwright](https://scholar.google.com/scholar_case?case=4964174066744569590&hl=en&as_sdt=6&as_vis=1&oi=scholarr#p551).

- â–ª

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-sigma' data-evernote-id='229' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)technicalâ€‹ â€œ409Aâ€ is a reference to the [section](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Code_section_409A) of the Internal Revenue Code that sets requirements for options to be tax-free on grant.

### Taxes on ISOs and NSOs

Typically, early to mid-stage companies grant [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options), which may be [ISOs or NSOsÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/kinds-of-stock-options).

- â–ª

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='230' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹When you get [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) and are considering if and when to [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise), you need to think about the taxes and **when you owe them**. In principle, you need to think about taxes you may incur at three points in time:

    - â–«at **time of grant**
    - â–«at **time of exercise**
    - â–«at **time of sale**
- â–ªThese events trigger ordinary tax (high), [long-term capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-and-short-term-capital-gains) (lower), or [AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) (possibly high) taxes in different ways for [NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) and [ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options).

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ The taxes at time of [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) will depend on the gain between the [strike price](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/strike-price-or-exercise-price) and the [FMV](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/fair-market-value-or-fmv), known as the **spread** or the [**bargain element**](http://www.investorwords.com/5414/bargain_element.html).

- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='231' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹ If youâ€™re granted [ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) or [NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) at a low [strike price](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/strike-price-or-exercise-price), and the bargain element is zero, then you may be able to [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) at a reasonable price without triggering taxes at all. So assuming the company allows it, it makes sense to [early exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/early-exercise-or-forward-exercise)  *immediately* (buying most or all of the shares, even though theyâ€™re not vested yet) and simultaneously file an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election).
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='232' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹ An [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election), as already discussed, is the choice to be taxed on the receipt of property even though you might have to forfeit or give back the property to the company. You can make an election on the receipt of stock, but you cannot make the election on the receipt of a [stock option](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) or an RSU because options and [RSUs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-units-or-rsus) are not considered property for the purposes of Section 83(b).

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='233' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹  [ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) are often preferred by startups, as theyâ€™re supposedly better for employees from a tax perspective. This assumes that (1) [AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) wonâ€™t be triggered and (2) youâ€™ll get a low [long-term capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-and-short-term-capital-gains) rate by holding the stock for the appropriate holding periods. However, often you either run afoul of the [AMT trap](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/amt-trap), or donâ€™t hold the stock long enough with the complicated 1 year + 2 year requirement, or the [spread](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/spread-and-bargain-element) at [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) is small or zero, so the difference wouldnâ€™t matter anyway. [NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) do have a slightly higher tax because of the need to pay [employment taxes](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/employment-taxes-and-payroll-taxes) on NSOs and not ISOs.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-natural-disaster-hurricane' data-evernote-id='234' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)controversyâ€‹ Overall, itâ€™s not clear the [ISO](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) is that much better for employees, so [many people](http://www.business2community.com/finance/nsos-better-isos-0826167#fz1HTCiOQxRyTr62.97) argue [for NSOs](http://www.startuplawblog.com/2010/08/11/top-reasons-nqos-over-isos/) instead.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-task-finger-bandage' data-evernote-id='235' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)confusionâ€‹ This is partly because [ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) can make it harder to meet the [long-term capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-and-short-term-capital-gains) holding period.[*](http://thestartuplawblog.com/the-problem-with-immediately-exercisable-isos/) Many people expect [early exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/early-exercise-or-forward-exercise), together with an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election), will help them hold the stock long enough to qualify for long-term capital gains. While this is true for [NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options), a murky part of the rules on ISOs states that even with an 83(b) election, the [capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) holding period does not begin until the shares actually vest. So if you want to immediately [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) an option and file a Section 83(b) election, and you might have [liquidity](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/liquidity-and-exits-and-liquidity-events-and-liquidations) soon, itâ€™s betterâ€”for those who canâ€”to do so with NSOs.

### The AMT Trap

When it comes to taxes and equity compensation, one scenario is so dangerous we give it its own section.

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='236' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ If you have received an [ISO](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options), exercising it may unexpectedly trigger a big [AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) billâ€”even before you actually make any money on a sale! If there is a large [spread](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/spread-and-bargain-element) between the [strike price](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/strike-price-or-exercise-price) and the [409A valuation](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/409a-valuation), you are potentially on the hook for an enormous tax bill, even if you canâ€™t sell the stock. This has pushed people into bankruptcy. It also caused Congress to grant a one-time forgiveness, the odds of which happening again are very low.

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ The catastrophic scenario where exercising [ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) triggers a large [AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) bill, with no ability to sell the stock to pay taxes, is sometimes called the **AMT trap**. This [infamous](https://www.nceo.org/articles/stock-options-alternative-minimum-tax-amt) problem has trapped many employees and [bankrupted](http://blog.sfgate.com/dgreenberg/2012/06/22/tax-advice-from-the-dot-com-bubble-beware-of-isos/) people during past dot-com busts. Now more people know about it, but itâ€™s still a significant obstacle to plan around.

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-new-circle' data-evernote-id='237' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)newâ€‹ In 2017, Congress passed the [Tax Cuts and Jobs Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_Cuts_and_Jobs_Act_of_2017) (TCJA), which increases [AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) exemptions and their phaseout thresholds. This means fewer people will be affected by AMT in 2018 than in prior years.[*](https://medium.com/@barryjk/the-tax-law-that-is-unintentionally-hammering-silicon-valley-employees-894a7b54ba8a)

Note that if your [AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) applies to events prior to 2008, youâ€™re [off the hook](http://www.startuplawblog.com/2009/04/03/whoops-i-didnt-pay-amt-on-my-isos-exercised-prior-to-1108-what-do-i-do/).

Understand this topic and talk to a professional if you [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) ISOs. The AMT trap does not apply to [NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options).

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

### Stock Awards vs. ISOs vs. NSOs

Because the differences are so nuanced, what follows is a summary of the taxes on [restricted stock awards](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants), [ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options), and [NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options), from an employeeâ€™s point of view.

- â–ª

**[Restricted stock awards](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants).** Assuming [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting), you pay full taxes early with the 83(b) or at vesting:

    - â–«

At grant:

        - â–ªIf [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election) filed, ordinary tax on [FMV](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/fair-market-value-or-fmv)
        - â–ªNone otherwise
    - â–«

At vesting:

        - â–ªNone if 83(b) election filed
        - â–ªOrdinary tax on FMV of vested portion otherwise
    - â–«

At sale:

        - â–ª[Long-term capital gains tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-tax) on gain if held for **1 year** past when taken into [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains)
        - â–ªOrdinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale)
- â–ª

**[NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options).** You pay full taxes at [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise), and the sale is like any investment gain:

    - â–«

At grant and [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting):

        - â–ªNo tax if granted at [FMV](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/fair-market-value-or-fmv)
    - â–«

At exercise:

        - â–ªOrdinary tax on the [bargain element](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/spread-and-bargain-element)
        - â–ª[Income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) and [employment tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/employment-taxes-and-payroll-taxes) withholding on paycheck
    - â–«

At sale:

        - â–ª[Long-term capital gains tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-tax) on gain if held for **1 year** past exercise
        - â–ªOrdinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale)
- â–ª

**[ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options).** You might pay less tax at [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise), but itâ€™s complicated:

    - â–«

At grant and [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting):

        - â–ªNo tax if granted at [FMV](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/fair-market-value-or-fmv)
    - â–«

At exercise:

        - â–ª**[AMT](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt) tax event** on the [bargain element](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/spread-and-bargain-element)
        - â–ªNo ordinary or [capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) tax
        - â–ªNo [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) or [employment tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/employment-taxes-and-payroll-taxes) withholding on paycheck
    - â–«

At sale:

        - â–ª[Long-term capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-and-short-term-capital-gains) if held for **1 year** past exercise and **2 years** past grant date
        - â–ªOrdinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale)

Mary Russell, a lawyer who specializes in equity compensation, recommends each form of equity be used at the appropriate time in [private companies](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies): [restricted stock awards](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants) for the earliest stage of a startup, [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) with longer [exercise windows](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise-window-or-exercise-period) for the early to mid stage, and [RSUs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-units-or-rsus) for the later stages.[*](http://stockoptioncounsel.com/blog/early-expiration-of-startup-stock-options-part-3-examples-of-good-startup-equity-design-by-company-stage/2017/8/11)

If you relish tax complexity, you can learn more from:

- â–ªThe [Tax Topics](https://www.irs.gov/taxtopics/tc427.html) coverage of [ISOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) and [NSOs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/incentive-and-non-qualifying-and-statutory-and-non-statutory-stock-options) from the IRS
- â–ªJoe Wallinâ€™s posts on the Startup Law Blog, â€œ[Top 6 Reasons To Grant NQOs Over ISOs](http://www.startuplawblog.com/2010/08/11/top-reasons-nqos-over-isos/)â€ and â€œ[Incentive Stock Options vs. Nonqualified Stock Options](http://www.startuplawblog.com/2013/05/15/incentive-stock-options-vs-nonqualified-stock-options/)â€
- â–ªInvestopediaâ€™s post â€œ[Get the Most Out of Employee Stock Options](http://www.investopedia.com/articles/optioninvestor/07/esoabout.asp)â€
- â–ªEquityZenâ€™s summary of the topic, â€œ[Understanding Equity Compensation And What It Means For Startup Employees](https://equityzen.com/blog/understanding-equity-compensation-for-startup-employees/)â€

### Taxes on RSUs

If you are awarded [RSUs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-units-or-rsus), each unit represents one share of stock that you will be given when the units vest.

- â–ª

Hereâ€™s the tax summary for [RSUs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-units-or-rsus):

    - â–«

At grant:

        - â–ªNo tax
    - â–«

At vesting/delivery:

        - â–ªOrdinary tax on current share value
    - â–«

At sale:

        - â–ª[Long-term capital gains tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-tax) on gain if held for **1 year** past [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting)
        - â–ªOrdinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale)
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='238' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹ When you receive your shares, you are taxed on their value at that time.[*](http://joewallin.com/2014/09/13/rsus-vs-restricted-stock-vs-stock-options/) If you are an employee, this means you may have to write a check to the company to cover your [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) and [employment tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/employment-taxes-and-payroll-taxes) withholding. Often, for U.S. employees, companies will withhold the tax in the form of shares such that no action is required by the employee at [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting) time.[*](https://www.schwab.com/public/eac/resources/articles/rsu_basics.html)
- â–ªIf you receive an RSU when the stock is of little value, you cannot elect to be taxed on the value of that stock when you receive the RSUâ€”you pay taxes at [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting) time, based on the value of the shares at that time.
- â–ª

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='239' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹  [RSUs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-units-or-rsus) present some big problems in [private companies](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies):

    - â–«You will owe tax when you receive the shares, even though they are illiquid.
    - â–«You canâ€™t minimize the tax impact of an increase in value of the underlying shares between the date you receive the RSU and the date it is settled.
    - â–«If you are an employee you will have to write a check to the company to satisfy your [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) and [employment tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/employment-taxes-and-payroll-taxes) withholding.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='240' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹  [RSUs](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-units-or-rsus) are less attractive than [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) from a tax point of view because you cannot make an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election) with respect to RSUs. By contrast, if you receive a stock option, as long as itâ€™s priced at [fair market value](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/fair-market-value-or-fmv) you will have no [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) upon receipt of the options, and your [income tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-tax) and [employment tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/employment-taxes-and-payroll-taxes) consequences will be deferred until you [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise), an event under your control for the most part.

### Tax Comparison Table

This table is a summary of the differences in taxation on types of equity compensation.

|     | Restricted stock awards | ISOs | NSOs | RSUs |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| *Tax at grant* | If 83(b) election filed, ordinary tax on FMV. None otherwise. | No tax if granted at FMV. | No tax if granted at FMV. | No tax. |
| *Tax at vesting* | None if 83(b) election filed. Ordinary tax on FMV of vested portion otherwise. | No tax if granted at FMV. | No tax if granted at FMV. | Ordinary tax on current share value. |
| *Tax at exercise* |     | AMT tax event on the bargain element. No ordinary or capital gains or employment tax. | Ordinary tax on the bargain element. Income and employment tax. |     |
| *Tax at sale* | Long-term capital gains tax on gain if held for **1 year** past when taken into income. Ordinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale). | Long-term capital gains if held for **1 year** past exercise and **2 years** past grant date. Ordinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale). | Long-term capital gains if held for **1 year** past exercise. Ordinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale). | Long-term capital gains tax on gain if held for **1 year** past vesting. Ordinary tax otherwise (including immediate sale). |

### Tax Dangers

Because they are so important, we list some costly errors to watch out for when it comes to taxes on equity compensation:

- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='241' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ If you are going to file an [83(b) election](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/83-b-election), it must be **within 30 days** of [stock grant](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants) or option [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise). Often, law firms will take a while to send you papers, so you might only have a week or two. If you miss this window, it could potentially have giant tax consequences, and is essentially an irrevocable mistakeâ€”itâ€™s one deadline the IRS wonâ€™t extend. When you file, get documentation from the post office as well as a delivery confirmation, and include a self-addressed, stamped envelope for the IRS to send you a return receipt. (Some people are so concerned about this they even ask a friend to go with them to the post office as a witness!)
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='242' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ Watch out for the [AMT trap](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/amt-trap) weâ€™ve already discussed.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='243' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ If you [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) your options, and your [income](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-and-ordinary-income-and-capital-gains) had been from consulting rather than employment (1099, not W-2), you will be subject to the [self-employment tax](https://www.irs.gov/businesses/small-businesses-self-employed/self-employment-tax-social-security-and-medicare-taxes), which consist of both the employer and the employee side of FICA. In addition to owing the normal [income tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/income-tax), this means you will owe the Social Security tax component (**6.2%**) up to the FICA wage base, and you will owe the Hospital Insurance component (**2.9%**) on all of your income.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='244' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ Thoughtfully decide when to [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) options. As discussed, if you wait until the company is doing really well, or when you are leaving, the delay can have serious downsides.

## [Plans and Scenarios](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/plans-and-scenarios)12 minutes, 20 links

### Evaluating Equity Compensation

Once you understand the [types of equityÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/how-equity-is-granted) and their [tax implicationsÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/taxes-on-equity-compensation), you have many of the tools you need to evaluate an offer that includes equity compensation, or to evaluate equity you currently have in a company.

In summary, you have to determine or make educated guesses about several things:

- â–ª

**Equity value.** This can be estimated by the value the company may have in the future, and the number of shares you may own.

    - â–«**[Percentage ownership](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/percentage-ownership-and-basis-points).** As weâ€™ve mentioned, knowing how many shares of stock or [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) you have is meaningless unless you know the number of [outstanding shares](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/outstanding-shares). What matters is the percentage ownership of the company the shares represent, including the [detailsÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/counting-shares) of how the total is counted.
    - â–«**Risk.** It is critical to understand [riskÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/stages-of-a-startup) in the business and [dilution](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/dilution) to ascertain the possible future value of equity. [This article](http://codingvc.com/valuing-employee-options/) from Leo Polovets provides some additional thoughts.
- â–ª**[Vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting).** Understand [whenÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/vesting-and-cliffs) you will receive the equity, as well as whether youâ€™re able to [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) stock options (and pay the associated costs and taxes), and whether you can do all this before your [exercise window](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise-window-or-exercise-period) expires.
- â–ª**[Liquidity](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/liquidity-and-exits-and-liquidity-events-and-liquidations).** Determine when you will be able to [sell your sharesÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/sales-and-liquidity), and if that is likely to be for a profit at that time. (We talk about liquidity of private stock next.)
- â–ª**Tax.**  [Tax concernsÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/taxes-on-equity-compensation) are inseparable from the value of equity. Know the tax implications of your possible grant, [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise), [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting), and sale, in terms of [ordinary income tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/ordinary-income-tax-and-short-term-capital-gains-tax), [employment tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/employment-taxes-and-payroll-taxes), [long-term capital gains](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/long-term-capital-gains-and-short-term-capital-gains), and [alternative minimum tax](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/alternative-minimum-tax-or-amt).

Thatâ€™s a lot, and even so, decisions are uncertain, but it is possible to make much more informed decisions once you have this information.

### What Is Private Stock Worth?

We now turn to the question of determining the value of [private company](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies) stock. Weâ€™ve seen how stock in private companies often [canâ€™t be soldÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/can-you-sell-private-stock), so its value is [difficult to estimate](https://www.investopedia.com/articles/fundamental-analysis/11/valuing-private-companies.asp).

The value of equity you cannot yet sell is a reflection of three major concerns:

1. 1.How well the company is doing nowâ€”that is, how profitable it is, or how many customers it is attracting.

2. 2.How well the company will perform in the future.

3. 3.How likely it is the company will be valuable as part of another companyâ€”that is, whether it may be [acquiredÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/sales-and-liquidity).

The first concern is relatively clear, if you know the companyâ€™s financials. The second and third come down to predictions and are never certain. In fact, itâ€™s important to understand just how uncertain all three of these estimations are, depending on the stage of the company.

In earlier stage [private companies](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies), there may be little or no profit, but the company may seem valuable because of high expectations that it can make future profit or be acquired. If a company like this takes money from investors, the investors determine the price they pay based on these educated guesses and market conditions.

In startups there tends to be a high degree of uncertainty about the future value of equity, while in later stage [private companies](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies) financials are better understood (at least to investors and others with an inside view of the company), and these predictions are often more certain.

### Can You Sell Private Stock?

Ultimately, the value of your equity depends on whether and when you are able to convert it into stock that you sell for cash. With [public companies](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/public-companies), the answer is relatively easy to estimateâ€”as long as there are no restrictions on your ability to sell, you know the current market value of the stock you own or might own. What about [private companies](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies)?

A [liquidity event](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/liquidity-and-exits-and-liquidity-events-and-liquidations) is usually what makes it possible for [shareholders](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-and-shares-and-shareholder-or-stockholder) in a [private company](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies) to sell their stock. However, individuals may sometimes be able to gain [liquidity](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/liquidity-and-exits-and-liquidity-events-and-liquidations) while a company is still private.

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ A **secondary market (or secondary sale, or private sale)** transaction is when [private company](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies) stock [is sold](https://www.cooleygo.com/secondary-sales-of-private-company-stock/) to another private party. This is in contrast to **primary market** transactions, where companies sell directly to investors. Secondary sales are not routine, but they can sometimes occur, such as when an employee sells to an accredited investor who wants to invest in the company.

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ Shares held by an employee are typically subject to a **right of first refusal (ROFR)** in favor of the company, meaning the employee canâ€™t sell their shares to a third party without offering to sell their shares to the company first.

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='245' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹ Private sales generally require the agreement and cooperation of the company, for both contractual and practical reasons. While those who hold private stock may hope or expect they need only find a willing buyer, in practice secondary sales only work out in [a few situations](https://venturebeat.com/2016/12/19/secondary-market-for-shares-in-pre-ipo-unicorns-is-booming/).

Unlike a transaction on a public exchange, the buyer and seller of [private company](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies) stock are not in total control of the sale. There are a few reasons **why companies may not support secondary sales**:

- â–ªHistorically, startups have seen little purpose in letting current employees sell their stock, since they prefer employees hold their stock and work to make it more valuable by improving the value of the company as a whole.
- â–ªEven if employee retention is not a concern, there are reasons [private sales](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/secondary-market-and-primary-market) may not be in the companyâ€™s interest. Former employees and other [shareholders](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-and-shares-and-shareholder-or-stockholder) often have difficulty initiating secondary transactions with a company.[*](https://www.wsj.com/articles/former-employee-wins-legal-feud-to-open-up-startups-books-1485435602) Private buyers may ask for the companyâ€™s internal financials in order to estimate the current and future value of its stock; the company may not wish to share this confidential information.
- â–ªCompanies must [consider](https://www.square1bank.com/insights/new-normal-secondaries-409a-valuation-process/) whether sales could influence their [409A valuationÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/409a-valuations).
- â–ª[Secondary sales](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/secondary-market-and-primary-market) are an administrative and legal burden that may not make it to the top of the list of priorities for busy startup CEOs and CFOs.

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='246' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹ However, participation in the [secondary market](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/secondary-market-and-primary-market) has evolved in recent years,[*](https://techcrunch.com/2015/10/14/selling-private-company-shares-2-0/)[*](http://www.industryventures.com/2014/12/02/employee-liquidity-good-for-private-companies/)[*](https://medium.com/@rizstanford/secondary-sales-in-vc-backed-startups-a-quick-primer-for-entrepreneurs-bdc25ea7f39a) and **a few options may be possible**:

- â–ª[SharesPost](http://sharespost.com/), [Equidate](https://www.equidateinc.com/), and [EquityZen](https://equityzen.com/) have sought to establish a market around [secondary sales](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/secondary-market-and-primary-market), particularly for well-known pre-[IPO](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/initial-public-offering-or-ipo-and-goes-public) companies.
- â–ªA few other secondary firms have emerged that have interest in certain purchases, especially for larger [secondary sales](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/secondary-market-and-primary-market) from founders, early employees, or executives. A company can work with a firm to facilitate multiple transactions. These firms include [137 Ventures](http://137ventures.com/), [ESO Fund](https://employeestockoptions.com/), [Akkadian Ventures](https://www.akkadianventures.com/), [Industry Ventures](http://www.industryventures.com/), [Atlas Peak](http://www.atlaspeakcap.com/), and [Founders Circle](http://www.founderscircle.com/).
- â–ªIn some cases, an employee may have luck selling stock privately to an individual, like a [board member](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/board-of-directors-and-inside-directors-and-outside-directors-and-board-members-and-board-seat) or former executive, who wishes to increase their ownership. Further discussion can be found [on Quora](https://www.quora.com/How-do-employees-in-startups-sell-stock-in-the-secondary-markets).

### Stock Option Scenarios

The key decisions around [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) are when to [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) and, if you can, when to sell. Here we lay out some common scenarios that might apply to you. Considering these scenarios and their outcomes can help you evaluate your position and decide what you should do.

- â–ª

**[Exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) and hold.** You can write the company a check and pay any taxes on the [spread](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/spread-and-bargain-element). You are then a [stockholder](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-and-shares-and-shareholder-or-stockholder), with a [stock certificate](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-certificates) that may have value in the future. As [discussedÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/how-equity-is-granted), you may exercise:

    - â–«Early, even immediately upon grant.
    - â–«Before [vesting](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/vesting) (if [early exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/early-exercise-or-forward-exercise) is available to you).
    - â–«Sometime after vesting.
    - â–«

After leaving the company, as long as the [exercise window](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise-window-or-exercise-period) is open.

        - â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='247' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹ Recall that the window is likely to [close soonÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/how-options-expire) after you leave a company, often 90 days after termination.
- â–ª**Wait until [acquisition](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/acquisition-and-sale).** If the company is acquired for a large multiple of the [exercise price](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/strike-price-or-exercise-price), you may then use your options to buy valuable stock. However, as discussed, your shares could be worth next to nothing unless the sale price exceeds the [liquidation overhang](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/liquidation-overhang).
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-diamond' data-evernote-id='248' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)cautionâ€‹  **[Secondary market](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/secondary-market-and-primary-market).** As [discussedÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/can-you-sell-private-stock), in some cases itâ€™s possible to [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) and sell the stock in a [private company](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/private-companies) directly to a private party. But this generally requires some cooperation from the company and is not something you can always count on.
- â–ª**Cashless [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise).** In the event of an [IPO](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/initial-public-offering-or-ipo-and-goes-public), a broker can allow you to exercise all of your vested options and immediately sell a portion of them into the public market, removing the need for cash up front to exercise and pay taxes.

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='249' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹ Note that some of these scenarios may require significant cash up front, so it makes sense to do the math early. If you are in a tight spot, where you may lose valuable options altogether because you donâ€™t have the cash to [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise), itâ€™s worth exploring each of the scenarios above, or combinations of them, such as exercising and then selling a portion to pay taxes. In addition, there are a [few fundsÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/can-you-sell-private-stock) and individual investors who may be able to front you the cash to exercise or pay taxes in return for an agreement to share profits.

Author and programmer Alex MacCaw [explores](https://blog.alexmaccaw.com/an-engineers-guide-to-stock-options#exercising_2) a few more detailed scenarios.

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

### Summary of Dangers

Because of their importance, weâ€™ll wind up with a recap of some of the key dangers weâ€™ve discussed when thinking about equity compensation:

- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='250' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ When it comes to equity compensation, details matter! You need to understand the type of [stock grant](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/restricted-stock-award-and-restricted-stock-and-stock-awards-and-stock-grants) or [stock option](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options) in detail, as well as what it means for your taxes, to know what your equity is worth.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='251' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ Because details are so important, [professional adviceÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/seeking-professional-advice) from a tax advisor or lawyer familiar with equity compensation (or both) is often a good idea. Avoid doing everything yourself, but also avoid blindly trusting advisors without having them explain the details to you in a way you understand.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='252' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ With [stock options](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/stock-options), high [exercise](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise) costs or high taxes, including the [AMT trap](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/amt-trap), may prevent you from exercising your options. If you canâ€™t sell the stock and your [exercise window](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/exercise-window-or-exercise-period) is limited, you could effectively be forced to walk away from your stock options.
- â–ªâ€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-alert-triangle' data-evernote-id='253' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)dangerâ€‹ If a job offer includes equity, you need a lot of information to understand the value of the equity component. If the company trusts you enough to be making an offer but doesnâ€™t want to answer questions about that offer, consider it a warning sign. Next, we offer more details on what to ask about your offer, and how to negotiate to get the answers you want.

## [Offers and Negotiations](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/offers-and-negotiations)27 minutes, 53 links

When a company offers any form of equity as part of its compensation package, there is a whole new set of factors for a prospective employee to consider. This chapter will help you prepare for negotiating a job offer that includes equity, covering negotiation tips and expectations, and specific reminders on what you can ask and what is negotiable when it comes to equity.

### Why Negotiation Matters

Before accepting any job offer, youâ€™ll want to negotiate [firmly and fairly](http://cefne.com/en/harvard-method-negotiation). Youâ€™re planning to devote a lot of your time and sanity to any full-time role; help yourself make sure that this is â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-money-bag-dollar' data-evernote-id='254' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)paidâ€‹[what you want](https://hbr.org/2016/12/think-strategically-about-your-career-development).

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-task-finger-bandage' data-evernote-id='255' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)confusionâ€‹ Itâ€™s perfectly natural to be [anxious](https://www.pon.harvard.edu/daily/negotiation-skills-daily/the-impact-of-anxiety-and-emotions-on-negotiations-how-to-avoid-misjudgment-in-negotiation-scenarios/) about negotiations, whether youâ€™re going through this process for the first time or the tenth. There is a lot at stake, and it can be uncomfortable and stressful to ask for things you need or want. Many [people think](https://www.forbes.com/sites/tanyatarr/2017/12/31/here-are-five-negotiation-myths-we-can-leave-behind-in-2017/#250ff99b15f9engaging) negotiating could get the job offer revoked, so theyâ€™ll accept their offer with little or no discussion. But remember that negotiations are the first experience youâ€™ll have of working with your new team. If youâ€™re nervous, it can help to remind yourself why itâ€™s important to have these conversations:

- â–ªNegotiations ask you to focus on what you actually want. What is important to youâ€”personal growth, career growth, impact, recognition, cash, ownership, teamwork? Not being clear with yourself on what your priorities really are is a recipe for dissatisfaction later.
- â–ªIf you arenâ€™t satisfied with the terms of your offer, accepting it without discussion can be tough not just for you but for your new company and colleagues as well. No one wants to take on a hire whoâ€™s going to walk away in just a few months when something better comes along. For everyoneâ€™s sake, take your time now to consider what you wantâ€”and then [ask for it](https://www.earnest.com/decision-making/articles/negotiating-job-offers-science-asking-want).
- â–ªThe negotiation process itself can teach you a lot about a company and your future manager. Talking about a tough subject like an offer is a great way to see how youâ€™ll work with someone down the road.

A Guide like this canâ€™t give you personalized advice on what a reasonable offer is, as that depends greatly on your skills, the marketplace of candidates, what other offers you have, what the company can pay, what other candidates the company has found, and the companyâ€™s needs. But we can cover the basics of what to expect with offers, and advise candidates on how to approach negotiations.

### Equal Treatment

â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='plain-diamond-outline' data-evernote-id='256' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)importantâ€‹ Companies can and should work hard to ensure that all candidates are given [equal treatment](https://rework.withgoogle.com/guides/pay-equity/steps/introduction/) in the hiring process, but inequalities persist.[*](https://iwpr.org/publications/gender-wage-gap-2017-race-ethnicity/) Workplace disparities in pay and opportunity span race and gender,[*](https://digitalcommons.ilr.cornell.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=2208&context=articles) with research focusing on inequality in the U.S. workplace,[*](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/07/01/racial-gender-wage-gaps-persist-in-u-s-despite-some-progress/) executive leadership and its well-documented lack of diversity,[*](https://aflcio.org/paywatch/company-pay-ratios)[*](http://fortune.com/2017/06/09/white-men-senior-executives-fortune-500-companies-diversity-data/) and the technology industry.[*](https://www.eeoc.gov/eeoc/statistics/reports/hightech/) Gender bias in negotiation itself is also an issue; many women have been made to feel that they shouldnâ€™t ask for what they deserve.[*](https://www.newyorker.com/science/maria-konnikova/lean-out-the-dangers-for-women-who-negotiate)

More effort is needed to end biases and close the wage gap. All candidates should take the time to understand their worth and the specific value they can add to a company, so that they are fully prepared to negotiate for a better offer.

### General Expectations

- â–ªMany companies will give some leeway during [negotiationsÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/negotiation-tips), letting you indicate whether you prefer [higher salary](https://hired.com/blog/candidates/salary-vs-equity-how-decide-whats-right/) or [higher equity](https://www.investopedia.com/articles/personal-finance/041515/equity-vs-salary-what-you-need-know.asp).
- â–ªCandidates with competing offers almost always have more leverage and get better offers.[*](https://www.shrm.org/resourcesandtools/hr-topics/employee-relations/pages/using-a-job-offer-as-leverage-is-no-longer-a-big-no-no.aspx)
- â–ªSalaries at startups are often a bit below what youâ€™d get at an established company, since early on, cash is at a premium. For very early stage startups, risk is higher, offers can be more highly variable, and variation among companies will be greater, particularly when it comes to equity.
- â–ªThe dominant factors [determining equityÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/typical-employee-equity-levels) are what funding [stageÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/stages-of-a-startup) a company is at, and the role youâ€™ll play at the company. If no funding has been raised, large equity may be needed to get early team members to work for very little or for free. Once significant funding of an A round is in place, most people will take typical or moderately discounted salaries. Startups with seed funding lie somewhere in between.

### Offers

â€‹Definitionâ€‹ When making a job offer, companies will often give a candidate a **verbal offer** first, to speed things along and facilitate the negotiation, following it with a **written offer** if it seems like the candidate and the company are close to agreement on the terms of the offer. The written offer takes the form of an â€‹![](data:image/svg+xml,%3csvg xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg' aria-labelledby='str-download-thick-box' data-evernote-id='257' class='js-evernote-checked'%3e%3c/svg%3e)documentâ€‹[**offer letter**](https://www.upcounsel.com/employee-offer-letter), which is just the summary sent to the candidate, typically with an expiration date and other details and [paperworkÂ§](https://www.holloway.com/g/equity-compensation/sections/documents-and-agreements).

Although companies often want you to sign right away to save time and effort, if youâ€™re doing it thoughtfully youâ€™ll also be talking to the company (typically with a hiring manager, your future manager, or a recruiter, or some combination) multiple times before signing. This helps you negotiate details and gives you a chance to get to know the people you could be working with, the company, and the role, so that you can make the best decision for your personal situation.

When you are ready to accept the terms of the offer letter, you can go ahead and sign.

Things to look for in the [offer letter](https://www.glassdoor.com/blog/how-to-read-offer-letter/) include:

- â–ª**Title and level.** What your role is officially called, who you report to, and what level of seniority your role is within the company.
- â–ª**Salary.** What youâ€™re paid in cash, in a year, before taxes.
- â–ª**Equity compensation.** You know what this is now.
- â–ª**Bonus.** Additional cash youâ€™ll get on a regular basis, if the company has a plan for this.
- â–ª**[Signing bonus](https://www.investopedia.com/terms/s/signing-bonus.asp).** Cash you get just for signing. (Signing bonuses usually have some strings attachedâ€”for example, you could have to pay back the bonus if you leave the company within 12 or 24 months.)

While the details may not be included in your [offer letter](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/verbal-offer-and-written-offer-and-offer-letter), to get full information on your total rewards youâ€™ll also want to discuss:

- â–ª[Benefits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Employee_benefits) like health insurance, retirement savings, and snacks.
- â–ªAll other aspects of the job that might matter to you, like time off, ability to work from home, flexible hours, training and education, and so on.

A few general notes on these components (credits to [Cristina Cordova](https://twitter.com/cjc/status/984094472190349312) for some of these):

- â–ªEarly stage startups will focus on salary and equity and (if they are funded) benefits. An offer of bonuses or a signing bonus are more common in larger, prosperous companies.
- â–ªBonuses are usually standardized to the company and your level, so are not likely to be something you can negotiate.
- â–ªThe signing bonus is highly negotiable. This doesnâ€™t mean any company will give large signing bonuses, but itâ€™s feasible because signing bonus amounts vary candidate by candidate, and unlike salary and other bonuses, itâ€™s a one-time cost to the company.

### Offers From Startups

Because startups are so much smaller than many established companies, and because they may grow quickly, there are additional considerations worth taking into account when negotiating a job offer from a startup:

- â–ª**Cash versus equity.** If your [risk tolerance](https://www.investopedia.com/terms/r/risktolerance.asp) is reasonably high, you might ask for an offer with more equity and less cash. If a company begins to do well, itâ€™ll likely â€œlevel upâ€ lower salaries (bringing them closer to market average) even if you got more equity up front. On the other hand, if you ask for more cash and less equity, itâ€™s unlikely youâ€™ll be able to negotiate to get more equity later on, since equity is increasingly scarce over time (at least in a successful company!). Entrepreneur and [venture capitalist](https://www.holloway.com/definitions/venture-capital-and-venture-capitalists-or-vcs)  [Mark Suster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Suster) stresses the need to [level up](https://bothsidesofthetable.com/this-is-how-startups-level-up-after-raising-money-328d17076515) by scaling pay and spending, focusing appropriately at each funding stage. In the very early days of a startup, itâ€™s not uncommon for employees to have higher salaries than the companyâ€™s founders.[*](http://siliconhillslawyer.com/2016/06/23/founder-compensation-cash-equity-liquidity/)

â€‹Â·Â·Â·â€‹

- â–ª**Title.** Negotiating title and exact details of your role early on may not matter as much in a small and growing company, because your role and the roles of others may change a lot, and quickly. Itâ€™s more important that you respect the founders and leaders of the company. Itâ€™s more important that you feel you are [respected](https://blog.shrm.org/blog/respect-and-trust-top-the-list-of-most-important-employee-job-satisfaction).
